## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a reactant concentration (dA/dt) as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the core problem of chemical reaction kinetics — finding the rate law governing how species concentrations evolve.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with reverse reaction or equilibrium offset)
- Competing reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)
- Half-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (diffusion-limited or surface reactions)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate coefficient)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant offset)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type rate law)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → autonomous ODE rate law, most common in well-mixed isothermal systems
- Negative sign of rate constant → consumption/decay of reactant; positive → production or autocatalysis
- Fractional power of concentration → indicates diffusion limitations, surface reactions, or complex multi-step mechanisms
- Rational function of A (numerator/denominator both involving A) → enzyme kinetics or heterogeneous catalysis with adsorption
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic behavior where both reactant and product participate
- Sum of different powers of A → parallel reaction pathways with different molecularities
- Explicit time dependence in rate expression → non-isothermal conditions, photolysis, or catalyst deactivation
- Square in denominator → competitive adsorption or strong product inhibition on catalytic surfaces
- Rate expression approaching constant at high A → zero-order regime indicating saturated catalyst or enzyme
- Rate vanishing at A=0 with concave-up shape → reaction order greater than 1, accelerating consumption at higher concentrations
